Requirement 10.2: Audit logs capture all user activities

[] 10.2.1.1-10.2.1.7 - Specific audit log requirements

check_cloudwatch_alarms pass

CloudWatch metric filters and alarms for security events:

  • Trail: management-events - Not configured to send logs to CloudWatch

PCI DSS requires automated monitoring and alerting for suspicious activities, unauthorized access, and modification of critical system files.

Recommendation: Configure CloudWatch metric filters and alarms for all required security events including: individual user access to cardholder data, administrative actions, access to audit logs, invalid access attempts, changes to authentication credentials, initialization/stopping of audit logs, and creation/deletion of system-level objects.

[] 10.2.1.a - Network access is logged

check_vpc_flow_logs fail

VPC Flow Logs status for each VPC:

  • VPC: vpc-0a8c26974d77ff661 (10.1.0.0/16) - Flow logs not enabled
  • VPC: vpc-0fd45e6a (172.31.0.0/16) - Flow logs not enabled
  • VPC: vpc-49abc32c (10.0.0.0/16) - Flow logs not enabled

VPC Flow Logs capture information about the IP traffic going to and from network interfaces in your VPC, which is crucial for network monitoring and security analysis.

Recommendation: Enable VPC Flow Logs for all VPCs to capture network traffic information.

Requirement 10.3: Audit logs record specific details

[] 10.3.1-10.3.2 - Required audit log content and format

Automated verification of CloudTrail standard log format:

CloudTrail logs include the following for each event (per Requirement 10.2.2):

  • User identification (userIdentity field)
  • Type of event (eventName field)
  • Date and time (eventTime field)
  • Success or failure indication (errorCode and errorMessage fields)
  • Origination of event (sourceIPAddress field)
  • Identity or name of affected data, system component, or resource (resources array)
Recommendation: CloudTrail logs include all required elements by default. For custom applications, implement logging that captures all required elements.
Requirement 10.4: Log storage and integrity

[] 10.4.1.b - Log file integrity validation

check_cloudtrail_validation fail

CloudTrail log file validation status:

  • Trail: management-events - Log file validation is disabled

File validation creates a digitally signed digest file containing hashes of log files, enabling detection of log file modification, deletion, or forgery after delivery.

Recommendation: Enable log file validation for all CloudTrail trails.

[] 10.3.4 - File integrity monitoring for logs

check_log_integrity_monitoring fail

Log file integrity monitoring:

  • CloudTrail log file validation is not enabled for any trails.
  • No AWS Config rules found specifically for CloudTrail monitoring. Consider implementing Config rules to continuously monitor log integrity.

PCI DSS Requirement 10.3.4 requires file integrity monitoring or change-detection mechanisms to alert personnel to unauthorized modification of audit log files.

Recommendation: Implement file integrity monitoring or change-detection mechanisms for audit logs.

[] 10.3.1-10.3.2 - Log access controls

check_cloudtrail_s3_access pass

CloudTrail S3 bucket access control:

  • Trail: management-events - S3 bucket: aws-cloudtrail-logs-366205796862-993f53a6 - Bucket policy appears to restrict access appropriately
  • Trail: management-events - S3 bucket: aws-cloudtrail-logs-366205796862-993f53a6 - ACL does not grant public access
Recommendation: Configure S3 bucket policies and ACLs to prevent unauthorized access to log files. According to Requirement 10.3.1 and 10.3.2, read access must be limited to those with a job-related need, and logs must be protected from modifications by individuals.

Requirement 10.5: Time synchronization

[] 10.6.1-10.6.3 - Time synchronization

check_time_synchronization pass

Time synchronization check for AWS managed instances:

Found 19 Systems Manager managed instances that can be monitored for time synchronization.

For comprehensive time synchronization in AWS environment:

  • AWS services maintain time automatically using NTP
  • EC2 instances should be configured to use Amazon Time Sync Service at 169.254.169.123
  • For managed instances, consider creating an association in Systems Manager to enforce time settings
Recommendation: Configure all systems to use NTP or similar technology for time synchronization. Requirement 10.6.1 requires time-synchronization technology. Requirement 10.6.2 requires correct and consistent time settings using designated time servers. Requirement 10.6.3 requires protecting time data and monitoring changes to time settings.
Requirement 10.6: Log monitoring and anomaly detection

[] 10.4.1-10.4.3 - Log review and monitoring process

check_log_anomaly_detection warning

GuardDuty is enabled in region ap-northeast-1, which provides log anomaly detection and threat monitoring.

GuardDuty detector 1ac543cd88948d65f809813b91366c78 is enabled and actively monitoring.

AWS Security Hub is not enabled in region ap-northeast-1. Security Hub can help aggregate security findings, including log-based alerts.

PCI DSS requires mechanisms to detect unauthorized modifications to logs and alerts for anomalous or suspicious activities.

Recommendation: Enable GuardDuty and Security Hub for automated log analysis and threat detection. Requirement 10.4.1 requires daily review of security events and logs from critical systems. Requirement 10.4.1.1 requires using automated mechanisms for log reviews. Requirement 10.4.2 requires periodic review of all other logs. Requirement 10.4.3 requires addressing exceptions and anomalies.

                                                        KMS Key Generation Capabilities

                                                        AWS KMS provides the following key generation capabilities:

                                                        • Symmetric keys (AES-256) that are FIPS 140-2 compliant
                                                        • Asymmetric keys (RSA and ECC) with various key lengths
                                                        • Hardware security module (HSM) backing for keys when using custom key stores
                                                        • Cryptographically secure random number generation

                                                        These automated findings provide evidence of key generation capabilities, but manual verification is required to confirm:

                                                        • Whether formal key generation procedures are documented
                                                        • Whether the implemented key generation methods produce cryptographically strong keys
                                                        • Whether key generation follows industry-accepted standards and best practices
                                                        Recommendation: While automated evidence is positive, verify through documentation that key-management policies and procedures specifically address the generation of strong cryptographic keys and compliance with industry standards.

                                                        [WARNING] 3.7.2 - Secure Key Distribution

                                                        Automated assessment provides limited evidence of cryptographic key distribution practices.

                                                        AWS provides secure key distribution mechanisms through TLS-encrypted API calls, IAM role-based access control, VPC Endpoints for private network paths to KMS, and CloudHSM integration for hardware-based key management.

                                                        Manual verification is required to confirm formal key distribution procedures.

                                                        Recommendation: Implement key-management policies and procedures that address secure distribution of cryptographic keys. Configure secure channels for key distribution and ensure methods maintain the integrity and confidentiality of keys.

                                                        [WARNING] 3.7.3 - Secure Key Storage

                                                        Automated assessment provides limited evidence of cryptographic key storage practices.

                                                        AWS KMS stores keys in FIPS 140-2 validated HSMs, and master keys in KMS never leave the HSMs unencrypted. CloudHSM provides dedicated hardware security modules for enhanced security.

                                                        Manual verification is required to confirm formal key storage procedures.

                                                        Recommendation: Implement key-management policies and procedures that address secure storage of cryptographic keys. Ensure keys are stored securely in the fewest possible locations and protected against unauthorized access.

                                                        [WARNING] 3.7.4 - Key Cryptoperiod and Changes

                                                        Automated assessment found limited evidence of key rotation practices.

                                                        AWS KMS provides automatic key rotation for symmetric keys if enabled:

                                                        • Key 4e445a81-0778-40ca-8079-21162a56fbd0 (alias/dotNet_MachineKey_20250318): Rotation DISABLED
                                                        • Key 852ba11a-cf60-421e-b000-9b2ffc1da86c (alias/WebConfig_ConnectionString): Rotation DISABLED
                                                        • Key 8db11ec0-d714-472f-9e04-68e3b685896d (alias/Canlead_CreditCard_Key): Rotation DISABLED
                                                        • Key 8fd10c27-60bd-4058-b714-ce474aebd47e (alias/how-cool): Rotation DISABLED

                                                        With AWS KMS key rotation:

                                                        • When enabled, AWS automatically rotates symmetric KMS keys once every year
                                                        • Previous key material is retained to decrypt data encrypted before rotation
                                                        • New encryptions use the latest key material
                                                        • Applications don't need to change how they use the key
                                                        • Asymmetric KMS keys cannot be automatically rotated

                                                        Manual verification is required to confirm whether cryptoperiods are defined for each key type and whether procedures for key changes at defined intervals exist.

                                                        Recommendation: Implement key-management policies that define cryptoperiods for each key type and include processes for key changes at the end of those periods. Enable automatic key rotation for AWS KMS keys where supported.

                                                        [WARNING] 3.7.5 - Key Retirement and Replacement

                                                        Automated assessment found limited evidence of key retirement practices.

                                                        AWS KMS provides key retirement capabilities through scheduled deletions with customizable waiting periods. Found 0 keys scheduled for deletion.

                                                        Manual verification is required to confirm whether policies for key retirement or replacement exist for various scenarios.

                                                        Recommendation: Implement policies for key retirement or replacement when keys reach cryptoperiod end, key integrity is weakened, or key is compromised. Ensure retired keys are not used for encryption.

                                                        [WARNING] 3.7.6 - Manual Key Operations

                                                        Manual verification required. Automated assessment cannot determine if manual cleartext key operations are performed or how they are managed.

                                                        AWS Key Management Service (KMS) generally handles keys in a way that prevents exposure of cleartext key material to users. However, some scenarios might involve manual key operations:

                                                        • Import of external key material into AWS KMS
                                                        • Use of CloudHSM key management utilities
                                                        • On-premises key management systems integrated with AWS
                                                        Recommendation: If manual cleartext key-management operations are performed, ensure they are managed using split knowledge and dual control. This typically requires implementing procedures where at least two people (each with partial knowledge) are required for key operations, and documenting these procedures formally.

                                                        [WARNING] 3.7.7 - Prevention of Unauthorized Key Substitution

                                                        Manual verification required. Automated assessment provides limited insight into controls preventing unauthorized key substitution.

                                                        AWS KMS implements several controls that can help prevent unauthorized key substitution:

                                                        • IAM policies controlling who can use specific keys
                                                        • Key policies defining permissions at the key level
                                                        • AWS CloudTrail logging of all key operations
                                                        • KMS grants for granular access control

                                                        Manual review of these controls and related documentation is needed to verify proper implementation.

                                                        Recommendation: Implement key-management policies and procedures that prevent unauthorized substitution of cryptographic keys. This typically includes access controls, role separation, oversight mechanisms, and audit procedures to detect and prevent unauthorized key changes.

                                                              [INFO] AWS Shared Responsibility Model for Physical Security

                                                              Under the AWS Shared Responsibility Model, AWS is responsible for the physical security of the infrastructure that runs AWS services.

                                                              Key considerations for AWS customers:

                                                              • Responsibility for physical security of the cloud infrastructure lies with AWS
                                                              • Customers are responsible for implementing logical security controls for their AWS resources
                                                              • Customers should document AWS's physical security controls in their PCI DSS documentation
                                                              • Customers should obtain and review AWS compliance reports (e.g., SOC 2, PCI AOC)
                                                              Recommendation: Document the AWS Shared Responsibility Model in your security policies, clearly delineating AWS's physical security responsibilities and your own logical security responsibilities.
